This Svāmī was born in the month of Āni under star Tiruvādirai. He became the pontifical head in the year Heviḷambi, in Mārgaḻi month, on a pūrṇimā day (January 1538) at Śrīraṅgam.

This Jīyar stayed at Śrīraṅgam for sometime and then proceeded to Kumbhakoṇam to offer worship to Lord Ārāvamudan. He stayed there for sometime and is said to have developed the temple premises by constructing maṇṭapas. Then he proceeded to Śrīmuṣṇam, Tirukkōvalūr, Kāñcī, Tirumala and then to Ahobilam where he is said to have offered worship at all the nine Nṛsiṁha shrines. He took up the task of constructing maṇṭapas, buildings steps leading to the shrines at Ahobilam, and dedicating his life to Lord Nṛsiṁha’s worship. He attained paramapada in the month of Āni in the year Subhakṛt (July 1542) on Kṛṣṇa caturthī. His Bṛndāvanam is at Ahobilam. He ruled the pontificate for four years and six months (1538 - 1542). [] His Taniyan reads as follows:

श्रीमन्नृसिंहवरदपराङ्कुशकृपात्रम्। श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं वन्दे श्रीभाष्यदेशिकम्॥

10. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Jīyar was born in the month of Vaikāsi under star Viśākā. He assumed the office of pontificate in the year Subhakṛt, Āni month (July 1542) on Kṛṣṇa pakṣa tṛtīyā tithi.

He set out on his religious tours (divyadeśasañcāra) visiting Tirumala, Kāñcī, Śrīperumbūdūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Tiruviṇḍantai, Tirunirmalai, Tirucci-ttirakūṭam totalling nearly forty-two holy shrines. He then left for Tirunārāyaṇapuram at the instance of the Lord, and stayed there till the end of his life. He left for his heavenly abode in the year Siddhārthi, in the month of Āni on Kṛṣṇadvādaśī (July 1559). He ruled over the pontificate for seventeen years (1542 - 1559).

His Taniyan reads as under:

वरदार्यगुरुस्तंबवणाब्जषट्पदम्। शठकोपमुनिं वन्दे शठारिप्रवणं सदा॥

11. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Vaṅgīpuram village in Tiruvaḷḷūr in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the month of Aippaśi under star Mūlam. He assumed [] the office of pontificate in Āni month, Siddhārthi year (July 1559) at Tirunārāyaṇapuram.

He visited the holy shrines at Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Kāñcī and Śrīraṅgam. He stayed for sometime at Śrīraṅgam,137 enlightening the people about Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy. After revisiting Tirunārāyaṇapuram, the Jīyar came to Śrīraṅgam where he spent the rest of his life in the service of the Lord and the propagation of Śrī Rāmānuja Darśana. This Jīyar occupies the pride of place among the Jīyars to have ruled the pontificate for a long period of 38 years and 9 months.138 He attained paramapada on Kṛṣṇapakṣa Caturdaśī tithi in the month of Citra in Viḷambi year (April 1598). His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam.

His Taniyan reads as follows:

पराङ्कुशकृपाऽऽसिध्पदाम्भोजैकधारकम्। श्रीनिवासमुनिं वन्दे मङ्गलानि तनोतु नः॥

12. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Bhāradvāja Gotra under star Pūraraṭṭh, in the month of Puraṭṭāci at Vaṅgīpuram. He became the pontifical head in the month of Citra in the year Viḷambi on Kṛṣṇa Pakṣa daśamī tithi (April 1598) at Śrīraṅgam. He then proceeded in his sañcāra to Tirunārāyaṇapuram. He

Then he proceeded to Ahobilam, Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Kāñcī and returned to Tirunārāyaṇapuram. He attained Ācāryan Tiruvaḍi in the month of Puraṭṭāci, in Āṅgirasa year on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ṣaṣṭī tithi (September, 1632 ). He ruled over the pontificate for 34 years and 5 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tirunārāyaṇapuram.

His Taniyan reads as follows:

श्रीपराङ्कुशयोगीन्द्र श्रीनिवासपदाश्रयम्। श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं वन्दे वेदान्तदेशिकम्॥

13. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This svāmī was born in Tiruvaḷḷūr (Vaṅgīpuram agrahāram) in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the month of Āni under star Uttarāṣāḍhā. He became the pontifical head in the year Āṅgirasa in the month of Puraṭṭāci on Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi (September 1632) at Tirunārāyaṇapuram.

He started his divyadeśa sañcāra visiting Śrīraṅgam, Tirumāliruñjōlai, and Āḻvār Tirunagari. He stayed for sometime there worshipping the Lord and paying his obeisance at the shrines of Nammāḻvār and Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa [] Svāmī.139 Following the instructions given by Nammāḻvār in his dream, the Jīyar gave discourses on Bhagavad viṣaya for more than a year, there. Then he proceeded to Śrīvilliputtūr, and after visiting Tiruppullāṇi, proceeded to Ahobilam and then decided to spend the rest of his life at Śrīraṅgam, enlightening his disciples in Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy through his discourses.

He attained paramapada in the year Naḷa, in the month of Aippaśi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ṣaṣṭhī tithi (October 1676). He ruled over the pontificate for 44 years and one month. He has the credit of having ruled over the Maṭha for a very large number of years next only to Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa. Hence he is referred to the Śrī Sannidhi cirlces respectfully as the Elder Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa Svāmī. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam.

His Taniyan reads as under:-

श्रीमन्नारायणमुनेः पदपङ्कजहंसकम्। वीरराघवयोगीन्द्रं वन्दे वरगुणार्णवम्॥

14. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āḍi under star Uttarāṣāḍham. He became the pontifical head on Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi in the year Naḷa in the month of Aippaśi corresponding to the month of October 1676. He stayed at

This Jīyar wrote the Ācārya Guṇādarśa140 in compliance with the request of his disciples who wanted their guru to expound on Guru Paramparāprabhāva. The Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā141 (ascribed by the Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā to the second Jīyar) is said to be authored by this Jīyar. He has also written the Gītārthasaṅgrahavibhāga, Gītārtha-saṅgrahasāra and Jijñāsāsūtrabhāṣya-Bhāvaprakāśikā.

He then proceeded to Kumbhakoṇam and then to his native place Pullambūtanguḍi, where he paid his obeisance to Lord Valvilli Rāma and Hemāmbhujavalli Tāyār. He visited many divyadeśas in and around Tanjore. Later the Jīyar attained Paramapada at Tirukkaṇḍiyūr on the banks of river Kāverī on an amāvāsyā day in the year Akṣaya in the month of Āḍi (August 1686). He ruled over the pontificate for 9 years and 10 months. His Bṛndāvanam is a Tirukkaṇḍiyūr.

श्रीवीरराघवमुनेर्निखिलस्यैकजीवनम्। समाश्रयेमहि श्रीमन्नारायणमुनीश्वरम्॥

15. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born at Eśānūr near Kāñcī in Thaṭṭai in Vādhūla Gotra in the month of Thai under star Citrā. He assumed the office of the pontificate in the year Akṣaya in the month of Āḍi (August 1686) on pūrṇimā tithi.

He travelled from Tirukkaṇḍiyūr visiting many divyadeśas enroute, like Tirukkōvalūr and then reached Kāñcī. He settled down at Kāñcī and discoursed on the Śrībhāṣya and other texts in accordance to the wishes of his disciples who resorted to his holy feet from far and wide. In the year Bhava, in the month of Puraṭṭāci (October 1694), this Jīyar attained paramapada on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ekādaśī tithi at Kāñcī. He ruled over the pontificate for 8 years and 2 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Kāñcī.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

श्रीनारायणयोगीन्द्रपदांभोजैकजीवनम्। भजे श्रीहृत्कल्पाणवीरराघवयोगिनम्॥ []

16. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Sōkatūr agrahāram (near Kāñcī) in the month of Mārgaḻi under star Mṛgaśīrṣa. He became the pontifical head in the year Bhava, in the month of Puraṭṭāci (October 1694) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa daśamī tithi.

After paying his obeisance to the Lord at Kāñcī, this Svāmī proceeded on his divyadeśa tour of the Southern districts. He reached Tiruvahindrapuram where he performed maṅgalāśāsana to Lord Devanātha and Lord Hayagrīva. It was at that time, that a scholar, named Tirunārāyaṇapuram Devanāthācār Svāmī resorted to the holy feet of the Jīyar. He gave discourse on the Grantha-catuṣṭaya before the Jīyar Svāmī and had his prapatti done by the Jīyar. Then he fervently prayed to the Jīyar to grant him the ochre robes and take him into the ascetic fold. Accordingly, he was initiated into the tūrīyāśrama (asceticism) and the Jīyar handed the Tridaṇḍa to him and named him Keśava Śaṭhakopa Jīyar and ordained him to write a Vyākhyāna for Tiruvāymoḻi. Obeying his Ācārya’s command, he wrote the Padinenāyirappaḍi and placed it at the holy feet of his guru. The Jīyar blessed his work and asked him to give discourses on darśana granthas.

Śrī Śaṭhakopa Jīyar then proceeded on tours to Tirukkōvalūr, Śrīmuṣṇam, Citrakūṭam, Teralundūr, Kumbhakoṇam and Tiruvindalūr. He stayed for sometime at Kumbhakoṇam during which time Kiḍāmbi Śrī Veṅkaṭācārya Svāmī paid obeisance to the Jīyar and gave philosophical discourses in his presence. [] The Jīyar attained paramapada in the year Bahudhānya, in the month of Vaikāśi (June 1698) on Śuklapakṣa aṣṭamī tithi at Kumbhakoṇam. He ruled over the pontificate for 3 years and 8 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Kumbhakoṇam.

His Taniyan reads as under:

कल्याणराजवमुनेः कृपापात्रं दयानिधिम्। सर्वशास्त्रार्थतत्त्वज्ञं शठकोपमुनिं भजे॥

17. Śrī Vīrarāghava Vedānta Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the month of Puraṭṭāci in Tiruveḷḷiyaṅguḍi under the Śatabhiṣak star. He became the pontifical head in the year Bahudhānya, in the month Vaikāśi, on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi (June 1698).

He proceeded in his divyadeśa sañcāra from Kumbhakonam to Śrīraṅgam and then to Tiruveḷḷiyaṅguḍi. He stayed for sometime there, doing maṅgalāśāsana to Śrī Kolavilli Rāma and Marakatavallī Tāyār. Later he proceeded to Śrīraṅgam and stayed there for sometime giving religious discourses at Rāmānuja’s sannidhi inside the temple premises. He gave discourses for twelve times on the Śrībhāṣya, fifteen times on the Bhagavad Viṣaya, ten times on the Gītā Bhāṣya and ten times on Śrīmad [] Rahasyatrayasāra.142 He was instrumental in providing the Lord with many divyābharaṇas.

The Svāmī then proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and paid his obeisance to the Lord there. He stayed for sometime at the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, then he returned to Śrīraṅgam and proceeded on a tour of the southern districts of Tirukkaṇḍiyūr, Kūḍalūr, Pullambūdaṅguḍi and Kumbhakoṇam. He also ordered many divya ornaments to be made for adorning Lord Valvilli Rāma and Lord Ārāvamudan. After worshipping at Tirumala, he proceeded to Śrī Ahobilam, the abode of nine Narasiṁhas. Then he went to Tiruvaḷḷūr to pay obeisance to Lord Vīrarāghava and Goddess Kanakavallī. Next in his itinerary were Śrīperumbūdūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Tirunirmalai and Kāñcī. Then he proceeded to Tirupputkuḻi, the abode of Lord Vijayarāghava.

This Svāmī fell ill there and attained paramapada in the year Pramādica in the month of Thai on Kṛṣṇapakṣa prathamā tithi (January 1734). He ruled over the pontificate for 35 years and 7 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tirupputkuḻi.

His Taniyan is as under:

श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं श्रीशठारिपदाश्रयम्। श्रीवीरराघवमुनिं वन्दे वेदान्तदेशिकम्॥

18. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the month of Puraṭṭāci under star Āyilyam in the family of Vīravalli at Tiruvaḷḷūr. He became the pontifical head in Pramādica year in the month of Thai (January 1734) on śuklapakṣa ekādaśī tithi. He proceeded from Tirupputkuḻi to Kāñcī and then to Śrīraṅgam where he stayed for sometime, giving discourses on Grantha catuṣṭaya. At that time, one Koil Kaṇḍāḍai Appan Svāmī resorted to the holy feet of the Jīyar and learnt the philosophical truths expounded in the Śrībhāṣya from him. Appan Svāmī was in charge of the Daśāvatāra sannidhi at Śrīraṅgam which was handed over to the ancestors of Appan Svāmī by Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī. Obeying the divine command, Appan Svāmī handed over the Daśāvatāra sannidhi along with its property, landed and monetary, to the Jīyar. It is also interesting to note that the silver vigraha of Lord Raṅganātha which is one of the many idols carried by the Jīyar in the silver maṇṭapa, in all his sañcāras (tours) and to which special pūjās and offerings are made day and night by the Jīyar, is the vigraha which had once adorned the house of Appan Svāmī and was handed over by his ancestor to the Ahobila Maṭha.

This Svāmī attained paramapada in the year Rākṣasa in the month of Āḍi (July 1735) in Kṛṣṇapakṣa ekādaśī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 18 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam. [] His Taniyan reads as follows:

श्रीमद्रराघववेदान्तमुनिवर्यपदाश्रयम्। श्रीमन्नारायणमुनिं श्रये श्रीभाष्यदेशिकम्॥

19. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Tiruvallikeṇi in the Naḍādūr family in the month of Māsi under star Maghā. He became the pontifical head in Rākṣasa year on the month of Āḍi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa navamī tithi (July, 1735). He proceeded from Śrīraṅgam and visited many divyadeśas like Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruvahindrapuram, Tirukkōvalūr, Madhurāntakam, Kāñcī, Tirumala and Ahobilam, then returned via Ghaṭikācala, Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Tirunirmalai, Tiruviṇanthai, Tirukkōvalūr, Śrīmuṣṇam and then to Pullambūtaṅguḍi. There, he stayed for sometime, performing maṅgalāśāsana to Lord Valvilli Rāma. He attained paramapada in the year Krodhana in the month of Māsi (February, 1746 ) on Śuklapakṣa caturthī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 10 years and 7 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Pullambūtaṅguḍi.

His Taniyan reads as under:-

श्रीमन्नारायणमुनेः पदपद्ममधुव्रतम्। श्रीनिवासमुनिं वन्दे वेदान्तद्वयदेशिकम्॥ []

20. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Piḷḷaippākkam village near Śrīperumbūdūr (the birthplace of Rāmānuja) in the month of Puraṭṭāci under star Mūla. He became the pontifical head in Krodhana year in the month of Māśi (February, 1746) on Śukla pakṣa tṛthiyā tithi.

This Svāmī proceeded from Pullambūtaṅguḍi to Śrīraṅgam and then to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and from there to Tirumala and then to Ahobilam. On his way to Ahobilam the Svāmī got the divine call and left for his heavenly abode, in the year Prabhava, in the month of Paṅguni (March, 1748) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa saptamī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for two years and one month.

It is not known for sure as to where exactly this Svāmī’s Bṛndāvanam is situated. The Śrī Sannidhi Guruparamparā simply states that it is in the northern region (Vada deśa).143

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीनिवासमुनिहृत्पङ्कजवेदान्तसम्भवम्। श्रीवीरराघवमुनिं कल्याणगुणमाश्रये॥

21. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Thaiyār agrahāram in Vaṅgīpuram (in Kāñcī district) in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the month of Paṅguni under star Hastā. He became the pontifical head in the year Prabhava in the month of Paṅguni (March 1748) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ṣaṣṭhī tithi.

This Svāmī proceeded to Ahobilam and then to Tirumala and from there to Tiruvaḷḷūr. He visited Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī, Tiruvahindrapuram, Kumbhakoṇam and Śrīraṅgam. During his stay at Śrīraṅgam the Svāmī gave discourses on the Śrībhāṣya before Vedāntadeśika’s sannidhi inside the temple precincts. Later, he visited Tirunārāyaṇapuram and the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, where he developed an intense desire to write a prabandha about his Ācārya. This gained divine approval instantly, by Garuda circling in the sky above. Accordingly, the Svāmī wrote Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī’s Aḍaikkalappathu comprising of eleven verses. This beautiful string of verses beginning with Ādimuraiyām extolling Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī’s greatness is included in the daily Nityānusandhāna in Ahobila Maṭha till this day. He also wrote Satsampradāyasāra which gives concisely the Ācāryavaibhava of all the preceeding Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha. He also wrote maṅgala verses on Lord [] Nṛsiṁha, Lord Kṛṣṇa and also a few songs to be sung during the cradle ceremony of Lord Kṛṣṇa (dolotsavam).

For sometime, the Svāmī stayed at Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then left for Śrīraṅgam. But on his way, the Svāmī fell ill and passed away. He attained paramapada in the year Īśvara, in the month of Kārthigai (November, 1757) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa caturthī tithi at Pāḷameḍu. He ruled over the pontificate for 9 years and 8 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Pāḷameḍu.

His Taniyan reads as under:

वेदान्तोदारवीरराघवमुनेर्नारायणश्रीनृधि- श्रीमद्घोरष्टदृष्टहास्ययमिनां कारुण्यवीक्षास्पदम्। विज्ञातोभयवेदमीलिहृदयं विद्वच्छिरोभूषणं वन्देयामुनदिनं पराङ्कुशमुनिं वैराग्यभक्त्यान्वितम्॥

22. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Gadādharapuram agrahāram in the month of Āḍi under star Rohiṇī. He became the pontifical head in the year Īśvara, in the month of Mārgaḻi (January, 1758) on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi in Pāḷameḍu.

This Svāmī proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and paid obeisance to the Lord there. Then he visited the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādivaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī and stayed for six months there. Responding to the divine call, he proceeded to Śrīraṅgam but fell ill on the way. He attained paramapada in Pāḷameḍu in the [] year Bahudhānya in the month of Āḍi (August, 1758) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa ṣaṣṭhī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for only 7 months, the shortest period of pontificate for any Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha. His Bṛndāvanam is at Pāḷameḍu.

His Taniyan reads as under:

विद्याम्भोधिरपारकृत्स्नमुनिराट्छिद्रेक्षदग्धाश्रितं व्रत्यन्तामृतवर्षिणं तनुभृतां त्राणाय जातोदयम्। क्षौण्यां ख्यातसमस्ततन्त्रकुशलव्याख्यातृताशालिनं श्रीनारायणयोगिवर्यमनिशं कारुण्यपूर्णं भजे॥

23. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Tiruveḷḷiyaṅguḍi in the month of Āni, under star Uttaraṭṭādi. He became the pontifical head in Bahudhānya year, in the month of Āḍi (August, 1758) on Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi. He proceeded from Pāḷameḍu to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then to the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī where he stayed for some time. He then proceeded to Ahobilam and after worshipping the nine Nṛsiṁhas, he started his divyadeśa sañcāra (tour) visiting Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tirunindravūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī, Tirukkōvalūr, Kumbhakoṇam and Śrīraṅgam. He then proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then to Śrīraṅgapaṭṭiṇam and settled down there. He attained Ācāryan Tiruvaḍi in the year Svabhānu, in the month of Thai (Februrary, 1763) on Śuklapakṣa daśamī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 5 years and 6 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgapaṭṭiṇam. [] His Taniyan reads as follows:

वीरराघववेदान्तनारायणपदाश्रयम्। श्रीवीरराघवमुनिं श्रये श्रितवत्सलम्॥

24. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Rāmānuja Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the Kalyāṇapuram Cakravartī family in the month of Citra under star Punarvasu. He became the pontifical head in the year Svabhānu in the month of Thai (February, 1763) on Śukla pañcamī in Śrīraṅgapaṭṭiṇam. He proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then to Śrīraṅgam and from there went to Ahobilam. The King of Gadvāl samasthān, Somabhūpāla, who came to know that the Jīyar was camping at Ahobilam, paid his obeisance to the Jīyar and invited him to visit his Kingdom. Complying to his invitation, the Jīyar visited Gadvāl and did pañcasaṁskāra to the King and his family. The king in return made generous endowments in the form of cash, lands and gold ornaments for the Lord.144 The Jīyar later proceeded to Tirumala and then to Tirunārāyaṇapuram where he gave religious and philosophical discourses. Then he wrote Śrīprapatti, Śrī Nṛsiṁha maṅgalāśāsana, Śrīstava and Śrīpañcāśat.

On his way to Śrīraṅgam, near Kokkarāyanpeṭṭai, the Svāmī fell ill and attained puramapada in the year Manmatha, in the month of Māsi (March,

  1. on Kṛṣṇapakṣa Tṛtīyā tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 13 years and one month. His Bṛndāvanam is at Kokkarāyanpeṭṭai.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

श्रीवीरराघवमुनिवृतिमोनिभूरि-श्रीमत्पदाब्जसममाश्रयलब्धबोधम्। श्रीवीरराघवमुनीन्द्रकृपावलम्बं श्रीमत्पराङ्कुशयतीन्द्रगुरुं भजामः॥

25. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āḍi under Svāti star. He assumed the office of the pontificate in the year Manmatha in the month of Paṅguni (1776, March) in Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi.

The Svāmī was well-versed in Tarka, Mīmāṁsā and other śāstras and was a Pañcakālaparāyaṇa in his pūrvāśrama. He gave religious and philosophical discourses on Śrībhāṣya, Śatadūṣaṇi, Nyāyapariśuddhi and Nyāyasiddhāñjana after becoming the pontifical head. He was well-grounded in jñāna and anuṣṭhāna and adorned the pontifical seat like a Yatisārvabhauma.

Jealous of the Jīyar’s erudition and scholastic achievements, one of his disciples dared to poison him.145 But the Svāmī’s benedictory glance was enough to make the disciple accept his crime and beg for the Svāmī’s

This Svāmī then proceeded to Śrīraṅgam and did maṅgalāśāsana to Lord Raṅganātha. He is said to have recited the following śloka while praying to the Lord146 —

श्रीरङ्गेशयः फणिपतिशयने दक्षिणां वीक्षमाणः ख्यातं श्रीताश्रुतीये प्रणवपरिणतं तद्विमानं च दिव्यम्। आद्यं व्यक्तं स्वयं च स्थलमतिशुभदं नायिकारङ्गपूर्वीं भूमेर्वैकुण्ठमेतत् जगति विजयते सहाजेन्द्रपुसितम्॥

The Jīyar proceeded on a tour of Southern districts visiting Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruvahindrapuram, Kāñcī and other places. Wishing to visit Badarikāśrama, the Jīyar proceeded northwards. He was confronted on the way by an evil sorcerer who threatened the Jīyar and his entourage. By invoking the Lord through Nṛsiṁha anuṣṭup-mantra, the Jīyar made the sorcerer ineffective. He fell at the Jīyar’s feet asking for his pardon.147

Unnerved by these threats the Svāmī proceeded to Gadvāl, where at a village named Sūrāpuram (Cuddapa district) he met a great scholar Kirīṭi Veṅkaṭācārya who challenged the Jīyar to a literary debate on Viśiṣṭādvaita philosophy. The Jīyar argued that a knowledge of the kāraṇavastu was

The king of Gadvāl, Somabhūpāla received the Jīyar with full state honours on his arrival at the capital. He stayed for sometime there and the king donated many ornaments to the Lord and gave a generous grant in kind to the Maṭha. Later the Jīyar proceeded to Ahobilam and after worshipping the nine Nṛsiṁhas, he went on a tour of Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tirunindravūr, Tiruallikkeṇi, Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī, Tiruvahīndrapuram, Tiruccitrakūṭam, Śrīmuṣṇam and Kumbhakoṇam. There he stayed for sometime and wrote Saccaritrartnāvali, Śrī Nṛsiṁhastava and Śrī Nṛsiṁhamaṅgala. He then proceeded to Śrīraṅgam and then to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and then came down to Pullambūtaṅguḍi and settled there. At that time, Tanjore was ruled by King Serfoji (1796-1833). Lord Nṛsiṁha appeared in the king’s dream and directed [] him to make endowments in kind to Ahobila Maṭha. Whereupon, the king invited the Jīyar to his royal abode and paid obeisance to him relating his dream to the Jīyar. The Jīyar was pleasantly surprised by the king’s donation of a village near Pullambūtaṅguḍi to Ahobila Maṭha for the daily worship of the Lord. Therefore the village came to be called Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. The Jīyar in turn, gave his holy sandals to the king who accepted and worshipped them with great veneration.148

The Jīyar then returned to Pullambūtaṅguḍi and ordered a Maṭha to be constructed at Nṛsiṁhapuram. He stayed there giving religious and philosophical discourses on Vedānta texts. Later due to old age, the Jīyar passed away. He attained paramapada in the year Prajotpatti, in the month of Kārtigai (30.11.1811) on pūrṇimā tithi. His Bṛndāvanam is at Nṛsiṁhapuram. He ruled over the pontificate for 35years and 8 months. This Jīyar is said to be an aṁśa of Vainateya (Garuḍa).149 Even today devotees are miraculously cured of their illness by praying at his Bṛndāvanam. It was also during his pontifical period that the largest amount of landed property was acquired by Ahobila Maṭha.150

श्रीवासवीरराघववर्यपराङ्कुशादि-रामानुजार्यमुनिभिश्चिरसेवनीयः। संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीश्रीनिवासयतिशेखरमाश्रयामः॥

26. Śrī Raṅganātha Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āḍi under star Pūram at Gadādharapuram in Śrīvatsa Gotra. He became the pontifical head in the year Prajotpatti, in the month of Kārtikai, on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi (21.11.1811).

This Jīyar proceeded from Nṛsiṁhapuram to Tiruādanūr, Kumbhakoṇam and then to Śrīraṅgam. From there he went to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and stayed there for sometime. The ruler of Mysore Śrī Kṛṣṇarāja Kaṇṭhīrava Sārvabhauma, sent his emissary to meet the Jīyar and to invite the Jīyar to Mysore. Complying to his request, the Jīyar proceeded to Mysore where he was received with full royal honours. Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha was placed on a golden swing (dolā) inside a silver maṇṭapa and many ornaments were donated by the King. A vajra vessel was also made for the Lord’s Tiruvārādhana. After enjoying royal hospitality for sometime the Jīyar started on his prerignations. [] The Jīyar went to Ahobilam and then to Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Kāñcī, Tirukkōvalūr, Tiruvahindrapuram, and then to Kumbhakoṇam. From there he proceeded via Śrīraṅgam to Śrīvilliputtūr. There the Jīyar was instrumental in building a Maṭha in the sannidhi street and also performing many renovations in the Āṇḍāḷ sannidhi. Then he visited the nine Tirupathis in South India, doing maṅgalāśāsana to the deities there and then returned to Nṛsiṁhapuram. Here, he arranged for the construction of a Bṛndāvanam for his predecessor, the 25th Jīyar and installed his image there. He also established an agrahāra (Brahmin settlement) nearby called Śrīraṅganāthapuram. Complying to the request of his disciplies the Jīyar wrote a manual on the daily rites to be followed by the Ahobila Maṭha titled Śrī Sannidhi Āhnika. He also wrote a few verses on Lord Nṛsiṁha. Due to his old age, the Jīyar left for his heavenly abode in the year Sarvadhārī, in the month of Mārgaḻi (20.12.1828) on Śuklapakṣa caturdaśī tithi. He ruled over the pontificate for 17 years and one month. His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. This Jīyar was the son of the 25th Jīyar in his pūrvāśrama.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीवीरराघवयतीन्द्रपराङ्कुशादि-रामानुजार्यकमलाब्धिरविप्रसिध्वर्यैः। संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीरङ्गनाथयतिशेखरमाश्रयामः॥ []

27. Śrī Vīrarāghava Vedānta Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the month of Vaikāśi, under star Aviṭṭam in Gadādharapuram in Ilanagar (Kāñcī). He became the pontifical head in the year Sarvadhārī in the month of Mārgaḻi on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi (10.1.1829).

He toured Pillambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr, Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruccitrakūṭam, Tiruvahindrapuram, Kāñcī, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tirumala and then proceeded to Ahobilam. After worshipping the nine Nṛsiṁhas, he stayed for sometime at Lower Ahobilam and paid his obeisance to Lord Prahlādavarada. The reigning King of Gadvāl, a Śrī Sannidhiśiṣya, paid his respects to the Jīyar and invited him to visit Gadvāl. Responding to his invitation the Jīyar visited Gadvāl and stayed there for sometime.

This Jīyar has many works to his credit. He has written the Vaikuṇṭha Vijaya Campū151 (a retaliation to Nīlakaṇṭha Vijaya Campū), *Caṇḍamāruta Vyākhyāna, Tātparya Ratnāvalī, Brahmasabdavādārtha, Viśeṣa Tarka Vāda, Vṛttisūtra in Vyākaraṇa, Vyākaraṇaśloka for Mahābhāṣya, Saṁkramaṇa-nirṇaya, Jayantinirṇaya, Strīsaṁskāraviṣayanirṇaya, Mūlamantrajapa-nirṇaya, Nyāsollāsa, Kṛpāsāgarastava, Daśāvarādirghagāyatrī-japanirṇayaśloka, Yativiṣaye sudarśanahomābhāvanirṇaya, Kṣiraṇa-

This Jīyar was a famous personage during his pontifical term. The rapport between this Jīyar and the King of Gadvāl can be understood from the fact when the Jīyar fell ill, he left the Ahobila Maṭha in charge of the King of Gadvāl and authorised him to find a suitable successor to the pontificate.152

This Jīyar attained paramapada in the year Khara, in the month of Āvaṇi, in Śuklapakṣa aṣṭamī tithi (17.8.1831). His Bṛndāvanam is on the banks of river Kṛṣṇā in Gadvāl district. He ruled over the pontificate for a short period of 2 years and 7 months. This Jīyar was the grandson of the 25th Jīyar and the son of the 26th Jīyar in their pūrvāśrama.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्री श्रीनिवासयतिशेखरलब्धबोधं श्रीरङ्गनाथयतिपुर्यपदाब्जभृङ्गम्। श्रीवीरराघवमुनिस्फुरितम्लिभृङ्गैः श्रीनाथभक्तिभरिताश्रयमाश्रयामः॥

28. Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the month of Āvaṇi under star Mūlam in the Naḍādūr family in Śrīvatsa Gotra in Tirukkuruṅguḍi. His pūrvāśrama name

There was an interregnum for a period of one year and eleven months after the passing away of the 27th Jīyar. The King of Gadvāl, who was given the charge of nominating a suitable successor to the pontifical throne, called for a vidvatsadas (a meeting of eminent scholars) to make his selection. The choice naturally fell on Tirukuruṅguḍi Svāmī who was well-qualified, with excellent communication skills to elucidate on the subtleties of the Viśiṣṭādvaita system of philosophy. He was able to establish his superiority in literary debates too, by winning over his adversaries with the greatest ease. In response to the King’s request, this Svāmī donned the ochre robes and became the pontifical head in the year Vijaya, in the month of Āni, on Kṛṣṇapakṣa pañcamī tithi (7.7.1833).

In the hierarchy of Ahobilam Maṭha Jīyars, this Svāmī is placed on par with Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, Śrī Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśa Svāmī and Śrī [] Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika. He is also said to have granted succour to his afflicted devotees through his mantric powers.153

This Svāmī proceeded from Gadvāl to Ahobilam, Tirumala, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Śrī Perumbūdūr, Kāñcī and Madhurāntakam where he stayed for sometime performing maṅgalāśāsana to Lord Kodaṇḍa Rāma and Goddess Janakavallī. He also gave religious and philosophical discourses to his devotees.

An incident is related in the Jīyar’s life, when a rich devotee who was proud of his wealth, offered many pomegranate fruits and gold coins to the Jīyar. In order to humble his pride, the Jīyar ordered that both be offered to the Lord and then distributed equally among the devotees who had gathered there. The rich devotee realised his mistake and fell at the Jīyar’s feet asking for his forgiveness.

Even when the Jīyar was at Madhurāntakam, he felt that his health was failing, and promptly appointed Lālāpeṭṭai Vajram Svāmī to look after the nityārādhana of the Lord who later appointed Ilanagar Gadādharapuram Śrī Cakravarti Svāmī to succeed him. The Jīyar attained paramapada in the year Durmukhi, in the month of Mārgaḻi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa saptamī tithi (29.12.1836). He ruled over the pontificate for three years and five months. It is to be noted

The Jīyar’s Bṛndāvanam is at Madhurāntakam.

His Taniyan reads as under:-

श्रीवासहृत्पतिवीरराघवहादिवेदान्तसंयमिमौलिस्त्सायकमौलिभाजः। संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीरङ्गनाथशठकोपमुनिं भजामः॥

29. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Lālāpeṭṭai in Vajram family in the month of Caitra under the star Citrā. He became the pontifical head in the year Durmukhi in the month of Kārthigai, on Śuklapakṣa navamī tithi (17.11.1836).

This Svāmī proceeded from Madhurāntakam to Kāñcī, Tirupputkuḻi, and then to Tiruppāṟkaḍal on the banks of the river Pālār. Finding his health to be deteriorating, he decided to stay there permanently. He called upon Ilanagar Gadādharapuram Cakravartiyācāriār Svāmī to become the pontifical head. Obeying the Ācārya’s command, he took to saṁnyāsāśrama under the name of Śrīnivāsa Vedānta Mahādeśika.

The 29th Jīyar wrote the Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁhasuprabhātam. When he was at Tiruppāṟkaḍal, the Svāmī fell ill and passed away. He attained paramapada in the year Heviḷambi in the month of Mārgaḻi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa [] caturdaśī tithi (10.12.1837). He ruled over the pontificate for one year and one month. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruppāṟkaḍal.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

विप्राम्भोधिसुधद्युतिव्रतिभिराट् श्रीवासरङ्गाधिप- श्रीमद्घोरष्टदृष्टद्युतिविरयोद्योगीश्वरैरेन्दहम्। रक्षाशिक्षणठारिसेप्यमिरक्षालोकितं सादरं विद्यावारिनिधिं पराङ्कुशयतीन्द्राख्यं मुनीन्द्रं भजे॥

30. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Vedānta Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Ilanagar Gadādharapuram in Śrīvatsa Gotra in the month of Mārgaḻi, under star Viśākhā. His pūrvāśrama name was Vidvān Cakravartiyācārya. He became the pontifical head in the year Durmukhi in the month of Paṅguni on Śuklapakṣa navamī tithi (15.3.1837).

This Svāmī proceeded from Tiruppāṟkaḍal to Kāñcī, Śrīperumbūdūr, Tiruvaḷḷūr, Tirunindravūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Tirunirmalai, Tiruvidavendai, Madhurāntakam, Tirvahindrapuram, and then to Kumbhakoṇam. There, he presented a golden kavaca to Lord Ārāvamudan.

Then he visited Pullambūtaṅguḍi and Ādanūr and stayed for sometime at Nṛsiṁhapuram. He was instrumental in constructing the bṛndāvanams for his pūrvācāryas who were enshrined there.

This Svāmī has ten compositions to his credit. He wrote Śrī Nṛsiṁhamaṅgalāśāsana, Śrī Nṛsiṁhamaṅgalam, Śrī Raṅganāthamaṅgalam, [] Śrī Śrīnivāsamaṅgalam, Śrī Gītācāryan maṅgalam, Śrī Śārṅgapāṇi maṅgalam154 Śrī Lakṣmīnṛsiṁha Suprabhātam, Śrī Raṅganātha Suprabhātam, Śrī Śrīnivāsa Suprabhātam, and Śrī Lakṣmīnṛsiṁha Prapatti. This Svāmī’s Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Suprabhātam is included in the Nityānusandhānam of the Ahobila Maṭha till this day.

This Jīyar then visited the divyadeśas in the Southern districts and returned to Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram and settled down there. He attained paramapada in the year Subhakṛt in the month of Puraṭṭāci on Kṛṣṇapakṣa caturthī tithi (27.9.1842). He ruled over the pontificate for five years and six months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Nṛsiṁhapuram.

His Taniyan reads as follows:-

श्रीवासकृत्पतिवीरराघवहादिवेदान्तदेशिकपराङ्कुशलक्ष्मणार्यः। संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीश्रीनिवासनिगमान्तगुरुं भजामः॥

31. Śrīman Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Śrīraṅgam in the Viñjimūr family, in the month of Kārtigai under star Makhā. He became the pontifical head in the year Subhakṛt in the month of Kārtigai on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi (7.12.1842).

Desirous of solitude, the Svāmī proceeded to a small hamlet on the banks of river Kāverī called Tyāgarājapuram and settled down there, worshipping Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha. The Svāmī attained paramapada in the year Parābhava, in the month of Paṅguni on Śuklapakṣa caturdaśī tithi (30.3.1847). He ruled over the pontificate for four years and four months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tyāgarājapuram.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीरङ्गनाथयतिवर्यकृपाब्धिसौधं श्रीवासवेदशिखरायदयावलम्बम्। वैराग्यभक्तिसुभृशद्गुणसागरं श्रीनारायणश्रितशिरोयतिगुरुमाश्रयामः॥

32. Śrī Vīrarāghava Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Śrīvilliputtūr, in the month of Caitra under star Pūraṭṭādi. Since his native place was Ādanūr, this Svāmī was popularly [] known as Ādanūr Aḻiyasiṅgar. He became the pontifical head in the year Parābhava in the month of Paṅguni on Śukalapakṣa pañcamī tithi (30.3.1847).

This Svāmī proceeded from Tyāgarājapuram to Kumbhakoṇam and then to Pullambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr and then to Śrīraṅgam, Āḻvār Tirunagari and the nine southern Tirupatis, Vānamāmalai, Tirukkuruṅguḍi, Madurai, Madhurāntakam and Kāñcī. Here, he visited the eighteen satellite divyadeśas around Kāñcī and then proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram via Tirupputkuḻi. He stayed for sometime there doing maṅgalāśāsana to Lord and Śrī. The local king Śrī Kṛṣṇarāja Kaṇṭhīrava Sārvabhauma sent an invitation to the Jīyar to visit Mysore. The Jīyar complied with his request and stayed for sometime at Mysore accepting royal patronage. Later, he proceeded to Colasiṁhapuram and Tirumala and then decided to settle down at Tiruvaḷḷūr, because of his age.155

The Svāmī chose as his successor a learned paṇḍit well-versed in the Bhāṣya and Rahasya Granthas called Parandūr Vaṅgīpuram Vedānta Tātācārya Svāmī, who was hardly 26 years of age. He was initiated into the saṁnyāsāśrama and was named Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika. The elder Jīyar attained paramapada in the year Pramādica in the month of

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीवासहृत्पतिवीरराघवहादिवेदान्तमानिलयवेदशिरोयतीन्द्रेः। संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीवीरराघवयतीन्द्रगुरुं भजामः॥

33. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Parandūr village in Vaṅgīpuram family in the month of Puraṭṭāci, under star Viśākhā. He was popularly known as Vaṅgīpuram Vidvān Śrī Vedāntācārya Svāmī in his pūrvāśrama. He was initated into asceticism and became the pontifical head in the year Pramādica in the month of Āvaṇi on the 10th day of the Śuklapakṣa (12.9.1853).

After assuming the office of the pontificate, he proceeded from Tiruvaḷḷūr to Śrīperumbūdūr, Madhurāntakam, Tirukkōvalūr, Tiruvahin-drapuram, Tiruccitrakūṭam, Śrīmuṣṇam, Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruvinnagar, Pullambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr, and Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. He stayed there for sometime worshipping at the Bṛndāvanam of his pūrvācāryas.156

He then proceeded on a tour of South India, going up to Rāmeśvaram and then to Śrīraṅgam. Later, he proceeded to Tirunārāyaṇapuram and visited the Bṛndāvanam of Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī . He then visited

It goes to the credit of this Svāmī for having built a sannidhi for Svāmī Deśika and installing his idol at Nāgapaṭṭiṇam. In his scholastic erudition, he was placed on par with Rāmānuja, Deśika, Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī, Ṣaṣṭha Parāṅkuśa and Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika. He was instrumental in adorning the Lord and Śrī at Tiruvaḷḷūr with new ornaments, and acquiring landed property for the temple there. He ordered the construction of a big building for Ahobila Maṭha there. His style of delivering lectures and the comparative ease with which he outclassed and won over his opponents in literary and philosophical debates, attracted the masses to him.

An incident157 is related in his pontifical rule which makes interesting reading and bears testimony to the Svāmī’s divine charisma. While on a tour of the modern Karnataka State, the Svāmī and his entourage were confronted by a group of dacoits in the thick jungle. The Svāmī is said to have informed the dacoit leader that he could take whatever valuables he wished, but only

The Jīyar seems to have enjoyed the royal patronage of the Mahārāja of Mysore. The Āsthāna Vidvān of the Mysore Kingdom was one Rāma Śāstrī who underrating the Jīyar’s erudition by his youth, invited him to a literary debate158, without paying due respect to the Jīyar. But, the Āsthāna vidvān was easily defeated and he fell at the Jīyar’s feet requesting his pardon for misjudging his scholastic achievements.

The Jīyar wrote the Guruparamparā of the Ahobila Maṭha titled Satsampradāya Muktāvali, based on the Ācārya Guṇādarśa and Sat Sampradāyasāra by the earlier Jīyars. He had also written almost half of his autobiography in that book. One of his disciples Tiruvaḷḷūr Thaṭṭai Kṛṣṇamācārya was instrumental in publishing that work.

The Svāmī attained paramapada in the year Pramādi in the month of Āvaṇi on Kṛṣṇapakṣa daśamī tithi (10.9.1879). He ruled over the pontificate for 26 years. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीरङ्गनाथशठकोपयतीन्द्रपादु-पद्मप्रवणचित्तमुदारबोधम्। श्रीवीरराघवयतीन्द्रकृपावलम्बं श्रीमच्छठारियतिशेखरमाश्रयामः॥

34. Śrī Śaṭhakopa Rāmānuja Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the village of Attipaṭṭu in his uncle’s house in the year Śrīmukha in the month of Kārthigai under star Uttarāḍam (November, 1813).

His paternal grandfather belonged to Iñjimeḍu village and had the title of Māḍabhūṣi. This Svāmī was brought up at his maternal grandparents’ place at Attipaṭṭu and hence he became known as Attipaṭṭu Jīyar. Reference is made to this Svāmī in the book Sārabodhinī, a commentary on Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra by the 42nd Jīyar. The relevant maṅgalaśloka reads as under: [] स्तुतिपुलकाङ्कितगात्रं नृहरेर्बोधाब्धुना लसन्नेत्रम्। वन्दे शठरिपुग्रामावरजसुनीन्द्रं मदीयकुलनाथम्॥

The Svāmī’s pūrvāśrama name was Vidvān Māḍabūṣi Śrīnivāsa-rāghavācārya Svāmī. In accordance to the wish of his Ācārya Śrī Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra he donned the ochre robes and became the pontifical head in the year Pramādica in the month of Āvaṇi in Kṛṣṇapakṣa ekādaśī tithi (12.9.1879) on his 61st birthday.

This Svāmī is described as Vayovṛddha (old in age) Jñānavṛddha (ripe in knowledge) and Śīlavṛddha (perfect in conduct) by his disciples.159 He was a pañcakāla-parāyaṇa and an epitome of a paramaikāntin. He was popularly called Ṛṣi Svāmī because he had learnt all the four Vedas. He has many works to his credit. They are as follows:

Śrī Nṛsiṁhaṣaṣṭipādavārṇanam, Adhikaraṇa Sārāvalī Vyākhyāna, Nyāsaviṁśati Vyākhyāna, Sāmānyaviśeṣādinyāyasaṅgraha, Kavihṛdaya-rañjanī, Ākāśāśrayasamarthana, Ānantya- nirṇaya, Brahmasūtrārtha- mañjarī, Maṇipravāḷa Gītāvyākhyānam, Sāradīpikāhṛdayam, Vikṣāraṇya māhātmyam, Maṇipravāḷa Vyākhyāna on Nālāyirappadi, Tiruevvuḷ vaimaḻi in Tamil, Aḍaikalappattu for Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha, Kiṅgrheśa stuti, and Vedagiri Varṇanam.

न चलति निजवर्णधर्मतो यः सम्मतिरात्मसुहृद्विपक्षपक्षे। न हरति न च हन्ति किञ्चिदुच्चैः सितमनसस्तमवेहि विष्णुभक्तम्॥

The Jīyar stayed at Tiruvaḷḷūr for sometime. Because of his failing health he could not go on religious tours, though he wished to visit many divyadeśas. During his stay at Tiruvaḷḷūr he decked the Lord Vīrarāghava with many ornaments and also ordered a golden chariot to be made for the Lord which could be used during festival times. The Jīyar Svāmī used to call Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha as Mahāsvāmī and Lord Vīrarāghava as Māsvāmī (Mā meaning ‘mine or my’ in Telugu, Mā also means Lakṣmī and Mā meaning the offering of sweet flour to the Lord on (amāvasyā) the new moon day). It is to be noted that the rituals of worship (pūjākrama) as devised by this Svāmī (viz., kaṭṭiyam, eccharika and anugraha) are still being adhered to, for Lord Vīrarāghava.

Having adorned the pontifical throne with great prowess, the Svāmī attained paramapada in the year Citrabhānu, in the month of Puraṭṭāci on Kṛṣṇapakṣa daśamī tithi (5.10.1882). He ruled over the pontificate for three years and one month. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीमद्वीरराघवदुहानिलिशोरवेङ्ककार्यात्मज- श्रीवासश्रुतिसीमयोगिकुलजिद्ब्रोगीन्द्रवीक्षास्पदम्। विख्यातं सपदिमादिगुरुराट्तर्ष्यं विपाञ्चित्तं वन्दे श्रीशठकोपलक्ष्मणमुनिं वैराग्यवाराकरम्॥

35. Śrī Raṅganātha Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Poṉvilainda Kaḷathūr in Chingleput district in Bhāradvāja Gotra of Vaṅgīpuram family in the month of Vaikāśi under star Keṭṭai. His pūrvāśrama name was Vidvān Nṛsiṁhācārya. He was entrusted with the job of looking after the daily rituals in Śrī Sannidhi in the time of Attippaṭṭu Jīyar.

Obeying his Ācārya’s command, this Svāmī took to saṁnyāsāśrama in the year Citrabhānu in the month of Puraṭṭāci (3.10.1982). He was well [] versed in Tarka śāstra and was an expert in delivering lectures on Śrībhāṣya and other Vedāntic texts.

After staying for sometime in Tiruvaḷḷūr, the Jīyar started on his religious tour, proceeding to Tirumala, Tirupati, Tirunindravūr, Tiruvallikkeṇi, Śrīperumbūdūr, Kāñcī and then to Tūppul. He also visited all the agrahāras in and around Kāñcī and then returned to Tiruvaḷḷūr. It was during this Jīyar’s time that saṁprokṣaṇa was done to the Lord Vīrarāghava temple at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

The Jīyar was of a generous disposition and no one who came to visit him and pay his respects went empty handed.160 The Jīyar is said to have done samāśrayaṇa to the 42nd Jīyar (of Iñjimeḍu) Vidvān Tirukkoṭṭiyūr Svāmī. It is also said that Piḷḷaippākkam Jīyar (37th Jīyar) looked after the affairs of the Maṭha during the Jīyar’s pontifical period.

He attained paramapada in the year Sarvadhārī in the month of Āḍi on Śuklapakṣa caturthī tithi (10.8.1888). He ruled over the pontificate for 5 years and 10 months. His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr.

श्रीमच्छ्रीवीरराघवद्रुतिभकुद्गुरुसद्वपादाब्जभृङ्गं श्रीमच्छ्रीरघुङ्गवमनगुरुशेर्खलधवेदान्तयुग्मम्। श्रीमन्नारायणाब्धुतिशिखरतारारातिरामानुजार्य- प्रेक्षापात्रं भजामो गुरुवरमनघं रङ्गनाथं यतीन्द्रम्॥

36. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Kāñcī district at Parandūr in the month of Āḍi under star Pūṣya. His pūrvāśrama name was Vidvān Vaṅgīpuram Raṅgācārya Svāmī. He became the pontifical head in the month of Āḍi in the year Sarvadhārī under star Svāti (13.8.1888).161

He stayed for sometime at Tiruvaḷḷūr, worshipping the Lord there and giving discourses on the Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy to his disciples. He was the brother of the 33rd Jīyar in his pūrvāśrama and was a famous exponent of Śrībhāṣya during his times.162 The Jīyar visited the following

The Jīyar proceeded to Pādūr at the request of his disciples and stayed for sometime there lecturing on Vedānta Philosophy. He attained paramapada in the year Viḷambi in the month of Mārgaḻi, on pūrṇimā tithi (27.12.1898). The Jīyar’s Bṛndāvanam is in the western prākāra of the Pādūr temple. His idol has been installed there by the 40th Jīyar later. He ruled over the pontificate for 10 years and 4 months.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीनारायणवेदमीलिपतिराट्पादारविन्दाश्रयं ख्यातश्रीशठकोपदेशिकमणेर्लब्धागमान्तद्वयम्। श्रीमद्रघुवरीणयोगिवरण्यस्यात्मरक्षाभरं सेवे श्रीनिधियोगिवर्यमनघं निर्बाधबोधोदयम्॥

37. Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Piḷḷaippākkam near Śrīperumbūdūr in the year Krodhi in the month of Māśi (March 1845) under star Pūṣya. His father’s name was Vīrarāghavācārya Svāmī, belonging to the famous Komāṇḍūr Iḷayavalli family. His pūrvāśrama name was Gopālācārya and he learnt the ubhayavedānta at the feet of his father. He had his pañcasaṁskāra done by the famous Tirupputkuḻi Svāmī (Mahāmahopādhyāya Kṛṣṇa Tātācārya). Completing Adhyātma śāstra first under the 33rd Jīyar, he studied next under [] the 34th Jīyar. Recognising his erudition, the 34th Jīyar (Attipaṭṭu Aḻagiasiṅgar) appointed him as the Śrīkāryam of the Ahobila Maṭha which post he continued under the 35th Jīyar also. He had his prapatti done by the 34th Jīyar. He learnt Divyaprabandham from a Paramaikāntin Śrī Śaṭhakopācārya of Kāyār.

Then he proceeded to the divyadeśas of the South doing maṅgalāśāsana to the Āḻvārs en route. He participated in the Brahmotsava at Āḻvār Tirunagarī during the month of Māsi. He developed vairāgya and distaste for worldly life and had his āpatsaṁnyāsa (immediate asceticism) done by his Bhagavadviṣaya Ācārya Pūvirundavalli Śrīnivāsarāghavācārya Svāmī. He had his preṣamantropadeśa from Teṅkanikoṭṭai Svāmī at Tiruvaḷḷūr in the year Heviḷambi in the month of Āḍi on pūrṇimā tithi under star Uttarāṣāḍhā and was conferred the name of Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa. After the Saṅkalpamahotsava, the Svāmī proceeded to Kāñcī. He came to know that the 36th Jīyar had attained paramapada and complying to the request of his disciples he became the pontifical head in the year Viḷambi in the month of Thai (31.1.1899).

The Jīyar proceeded to Tiruvahindrapuram where he restored the utsavas in the temple after settling the dispute among the Śrīvaiṣṇavas there.163

His Taniyan reads as under:

अस्त्यत्रैव विशेषो बुध इति शठजित्सूनुहृन्मान्या मुनिभ्या मेकीभूयोदितस्यामिह निरुपाधिकं प्रेषितं सद्गुरुभ्याम्। वेदान्तद्वन्द्वमन्त्रप्रविविदिषुमुखैः शिक्षितं शान्तिगुप्त्यैः आदर्शं श्रीवीरराघवशठमथनगुरुं संयमीन्द्रं भजामि॥

38. Śrī Śrīnivāsa Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in the year Siddhārthi in the month of Thai on Śukla dvādaśī under star Tiruvādirai (Janurary 1860) at Kumbhakoṇam. His pūrvāśrama name was Tirukkuḍantai Ilanagar Gadādharapuram Śrīvatsāṅka Vidvān Cakravarthi Veṅkaṭācārya Svāmī. He was well-versed in Tarkaśāstra and had the good fortune of delivering lectures on Vedānta in the immediate presence of the 37th Jīyar and won accolades from him. As there was an interregnum of five and half years between the previous Jīyar and this Jīyar, the daily rituals of the Maṭha were carried out by the Śrīkāryam svāmī. [] The disciples appealed to the Government to appoint a head to the Ahobila Maṭha. The British Governor ordered the preparation of electoral rolls of the Maṭha’s disciples and after the casting of votes, it was found that the majority favoured the Gadādharapuram Svāmī to be the head of the Maṭha.

The Maṭha rose once again to become the centre of influence and revered seat of learning. The Jīyar became the pontifical head in the year Viśvāvasu in the month of Āḍi in pūrṇimā tithi under star Uttarāḍham (17.7.1905) at Nṛsiṁhapuram. He stayed for sometime there enlightening his disciples on Granthacatuṣṭaya and doing pañcasaṁskāra and prapatti to his devotees. He proceeded on sañcāra to Pullambūtaṅguḍi, Ādanūr, Kumbhakoṇam, Tiruvinnagar, Teralundūr, Tiruviṇḍalūr, Tirukkaṇḍiyūr, Tanjore, Appakūḍathān, Anbil, Vaḍuvūr, Tiruppuliyūr and Tirukkaṇṇapuram.

A devotee from north named Bālamukundācārya became his disciple and it was with his help that the Uttara Ahobila Maṭha was established at Puṣkaram. He also renovated a number of Maṭha-buildings and Bṛndāvanams of previous Jīyars. Knowing that his end was nearing, he appointed a learned Vyākaraṇa Vidvān Raṅgācārya Svāmī as his successor. He attained paramapada in the year Saumya, in the month of Citra, on Kṛṣṇapakṣa aṣṭamī tithi (12.5.1909). His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrī Nṛsiṁhapuram. His idol was installed by the 40th Jīyar later. There are two available works about this Jīyar. They are [] Kārakkurichi Vaṅgīpuram Vidvān and Vaibhava Prakāśikā by Vaṅgīpuram Raṅgācārya Svāmī.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीमच्छठारिजिह्वर्यवीरराघवशठारियतिशेखरदेशिकेन्द्रः। संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं श्रीश्रीनिवासशठकोपमुनिं भजामः॥

39. Śrī Parāṅkuśa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Rājamannārkōil (Mannārguḍi) in Urupattūr Cakravartī family in the month of Viśākhā under star Bharaṇi. He became the pontifical head in the year Saumya, in the month of Viśākhā on Śuklapakṣa dvitīyā tithi (21.5.1909). He was known in his pūrvāśrama as Vyākaraṇa Raṅgācārya. He took to the ochre robes at the instance of the 38th Jīyar. He visited Pullambūtaṅguḍi Ādanūr, and Rājamannārkōil. He renovated the Maṭha at Mannārguḍi and was instrumental in making a silver maṇḍapa for Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha. He also ordered the construction of the northern wall at the temple of Lord Vīrarāghava at Tiruvaḷḷūr. He performed pañcasaṁskāra and bharanyāsa to his devotees and gave lectures on philosophy and religion as propounded in the granthacatuṣṭaya.

Feeling that his health was failing, he called upon Kārakkuricci Vidvān Veṅkaṭakṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī to take to the ascetic order and succeed him. He named his successor Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa. He attained paramapada in the year Rākṣasa in the month of Viśākhā in Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi

[] (20.5.1915). His Bṛndāvanam is at Mannārguḍi. He ruled the pontificate for six years.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीवीरराघवयतीन्द्रपदाब्जभृङ्गं श्रीमच्छठारियतित्त्रयं कृपाप्तबोधम्। श्री श्रीनिवासशठजिह्वलिपुर्यधीशान् पराङ्कुशयतीन्द्रगुरुं भजामः॥

40. Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Kārakkuricci Agrahāram on the banks of the river Tāmraparaṇī in the Vaṅgīpuram family in the year Virodhikṛt in the month of Mārgaḻi under star Viśākhā. He became the pontifical head in the year Pramādica in the month of Caitra under star Pūṣya (17.4.1913). After the 39th Jīyar attained paramapada in May 1915, this Svāmī proceeded on his divyadeśasañcāra to Śrīraṅgam, Āḻvār Tirunagari, Tirumāliruñjōlai and then proceeded to Hyderabad.

During that period, Ahobilam had become inaccessible because of the fear of dacoits and evil spirits. It should be said to the credit of this Svāmī that he was able to allay these fears of the devotees by his mantric powers. He visited Ahobilam and performed worship to the Nava Nṛsiṁhas there. Many devotees resorted to his holy feet for freedom from miseries of this world and bliss in the world thereafter. He ordered many gold and silver vessels to be made, which were utilised for the worship of the Lord. He built Maṭhas at many places and was instrumental in making the Maṭha rich and prosperous.

[] He wrote the Maṇipravāḷa Dīpikā which elucidates in simple term, the philosophical truths found in the Śrībhāṣya. He also wrote the Satsampradāya Prakāśikā and Śrībhāṣya dūṣaṇaparihāra.164 He also established an Agrahāra called Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopapuram. Many treatises have been written extolling the Jīyar’s erudition - Yatīndra Guṇadarpaṇa, Śrī Raṅganātha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika Śatakam and Paramācārya Navaka. His devotion to Lord Nṛsiṁha earned accolades for him from his disciples who lovingly called him “Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Divya Pādukā Sevaka.”

He visited Tirumala, Tirunārāyaṇapuram, Madurai and Tuvarimān. Realising that his health was failing, he called upon one of his disciples, Śrī Gopāla Rāmabhadrācārya Svāmī to succeed him as the pontifical head. He attained paramapada in the year Dundubhi, in the month of Thai on Kṛṣṇapakṣa trayodaśī tithi (14.1.1923). His Bṛndāvanam is at Tuvarimān agrahara. He ruled the pontificate for 9 years and 9 months.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीमच्छठारियतिशेखरलब्धबोधं श्रीरङ्गनाथयतिपुर्यकृपेकपाम्। श्रीमत्पराङ्कुशयतीन्द्रदयावलम्बं श्रीरङ्गनाथशठकोपमुनिं भजामः॥

[]

41. Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Kārakkuricci agrahāram in Vādhūla gotra in the year Ānanda in the month of Mārgaḻi under Pūraṭṭādi star (Dec. 1854). His pūrvāśrama name was Taṭṭai Gopāla Rāmabhadrācārya Svāmī. He became the pontifical head in the year Dundubi in the month of Thai (17.1.1923). He was the oldest Jīyar to became the pontifical head of Ahobila Maṭha. It is to be noted that even at this advanced age, this Svāmī performed his daily duties (nityakarmas) to perfection. He gave religious discourses on the granthacatuṣṭaya as also on Nyāyasiddhāñjana and Śatadūṣaṇī. He travelled from Tuvarimān up to Rāmeśvaram in the South and Tirumala in the North. Taking into consideration his age and the prevailing mode of transport and poor road conditions, his divyadeśa sañcāra performing maṅgalāśāsana to the Lord and doing pañcasaṁskāra should be commended. He has authored the following works: Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Dhyānasopāna, Śrī Vedapādāśīstava, Daśāvatāra Vedapādastava, Nityaprārthanākārikāvalī, Ācāryadinacaryā and Śrī Mahāsvāmigadya (on the 34th Jīyar).

The Jīyar was able to acquire nearly two and a half lakh Rupees worth of land for the Ahobila Maṭha. He ordered the construction of new buildings for Ahobila Maṭha at Tirumala, Tiruppullāṇi and Vaḍuvūr. He installed the idols of the 33rd and 34th Jīyars in the silver maṇḍapa. He also installed the idol of 40th Jīyar and also his own image at Tiruvaḷḷūr. He also made anew

[] the Śrī Śaṭhāri in the silver maṇṭapa. Finding his health to be failing, he appointed Māḍabhūṣi Iñjimeḍu Vidvān Raṅganāthācārya as his successor after initiating him into the ascetic order with full honours. He was named Śrī Raṅga Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika. However, he recovered soon and for nearly 13 years both the Jīyars adorned the Ahobila Maṭha. He attained paramapada on Śuklapakṣa pañcamī tithi. His Bṛndāvanam is at Daśāvatāra sannidhi at Śrīraṅgam.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीमच्छठारिंशठकोपयतीन्द्ररङ्ग-कार्यात्मजातमुनिभ्यः गुरुसार्वभौमैः। संप्रेक्षितं करुणया परिपूर्णबोधं लक्ष्मींनृसिंहशठकोपमुनिं भजामः॥

42. Śrī Śrīraṅga Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Iñjimeḍu in Bhāradvāja Gotra in the year Bahudhānya in the month of Thai under star Uttarāṣāḍha (21.1.1879). He was known in his pūrvāśrama as Vidvān Iñjimeḍu Raṅganāthācārya. He had his Vedāntic teachings under Śrīmuṣṇam Svāmī (Svarṇam Kṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī) and had bharanyāsa done by him. In recognition of this Svāmī’s erudition he was appointed as the Āsthāna vidvān by the 41st Jīyar. Under instructions from his guru, he wrote sampradāya granthas like Uktiniṣṭhābharaṇam, Nyāsaniṣṭhāmīmāṁsā and also vyākhyāna on the Rahasyatrayasāra called the Sārabodhinī. He also wrote śrāddhamantrabhāṣyam, Upākarmanirṇaya, Kṛttikādīpanirṇaya, Śrīvaiṣṇavasadācāranirṇaya and *Gītārthasaṅgra-

[] havyākhyāna. He wrote a bhūmikā (Preface) for Tattvatīkā and Viśiṣṭādvaita Kośa (a dictionary of Viśiṣṭādvaita terms). He was initiated into asceticism in the year Śukla in the month of Caitra (April 1929). He became the pontifical head in the year Viṣu, in the month of Aippaśi (24.10.1941). He was instrumental in establishing a Vedapāṭhaśālā at Madhurāntakam and also bringing out a monthly journal of Ahobila Maṭha, Śrī Nṛsiṁhapriyā and in establishing a Maṭha at Bombay. The Veda Pāṭhaśālā has since developed into a famous centre of learning and is flourishing well in present day, and is sought after by young students eager to learn the Vedas. The Monthly Journal is having a wide circulation in the present day. The Chief Editor of the journal is the Ahobila Maṭha Jīyar and his editorial provides interesting reading to students of philosophy and religion and laymen alike. The Ahobila Maṭha at Bombay (Chembūr) is the centre of attraction to the Maṭha’s devotees there, and is flourishing well under the patronage of Śrīvaiṣṇava Śrīsannidhiśiṣyas.

He travelled from Śrīraṅgam to Hyderabad and then to Tirunārāyaṇapuram, Kāñcī and Tiruvaḷḷūr. Finding that his health was failing, he appointed Paruthipaṭṭu Vaṅgīpuram Vidvān Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁhācārya Svāmī as his successor who was formally initiated into the ascetic fold in Vikṛti year in the month of Thai (7.2.1951). For two years both the Jīyars adorned the Ahobila Maṭha and enlightened the disciples in Śrīvaiṣṇava Sampradāya. The

[] elder Jīyar attained paramapada in the year Nandana, in the month of Māsi in Kṛṣṇapakṣa prathamā tithi (1.3.1953). His Bṛndāvanam is at Tiruvaḷḷūr. He ruled the pontificate for twenty-four years and one month.

Śrī Pādūr Purāṇam Svāmī (Śrī Rāghavācārya) has written a work called Vaibhava Sudhā in 500 verses about this Svāmī.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीरङ्गेशयतीन्दुना करुणास्री स्रावितिं प्रेषितं ख्यातश्रीरङ्गसिंहकारिमुनिनाऽऽबुद्धजेन्द्रिन्द्रम्। दान्तिशान्तिदयादिभिः शुभगुणैर्भान्तं बुधाग्रेसरं श्रीमद्रङ्गशठारियोगिनृपतिं श्रेयोनिधिं संश्रये॥

43. Śrī Vīrarāghava Śaṭhakopa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born to Devanārvilāham Vidvān Paruthipaṭṭu Vaṅgīpuram Tiruvenkaṭācārya Svāmī in the year Plava, in the month of Kṛttikā under star Pūrāḍa. His pūrvāśrama name was Vidvān Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁhācārya Svāmī. He graduated from Tiruvaiyāru College taking his degree in Tarka and was awarded the Tarka Śiromaṇi title. He was also the Principal of Madhurāntakam College. He was a pañcakāla parāyaṇa who considered his own house to be a temple. He took to asceticism in Vikṛti year in the month of Thai (9.2..1951). He travelled from Rāmeśvaram in the south to Himālayas in the north and performed one of his cāturmāsyavratas at Ṛṣīkeśa. He built Vedapāṭhaśālās at Madhurāntakam and Pādūr and renovated the Rājagopuram at Pullambūtaṅguḍi and Tiruvaḷḷūr. He renovated the

[] Ahobila Maṭhas at Cuddappa, Vānamāmalai and Tirukkōṭṭiyūr. Many golden utensils were ordered to be made for the worship of Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha. A golden palanquin was also made for the Lord.

The Jīyar contributed many articles to journals like Vedāntadīpikā and Śrī Nṛsiṁhapriyā and also published some works of Attipaṭṭu Jīyar. After finishing his cāturmāsyavrata at Ṛṣīkeśa, the Jīyar came to Delhi, where he stayed for sometime doing pañcasaṁskāra and prapatti to those who resorted to his holy feet.

While returning South from Delhi, the Jīyar fell ill and attained paramapada at Naimiśāraṇya in the year Hemalamba, in the month of Kṛttikā on Śuklapakṣa tṛtīya tithi (24.11.1957). His Bṛndāvanam is at Naimiśāraṇya. He was the only Jīyar to have travelled so far across the length and breadth of India. He ruled the pontificate for five years and ten months.

His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीमत् श्रीरङ्घपूणवीरराघवारिपुणा संयमीन्द्रेण दृब् न्यस्तात्मानं नृसिंहं नृहरिश्ठजिह्वागिणेतुः प्रसादात्। प्राज्ञ-श्रीरङ्गकारिप्रभवयतिपतिः प्रापितलक्ष्मींनृसिंहा- स्थानं सेवे यतीन्द्रं सकलगुणनिधिं वीरराघ्वशठारिम्॥

44. Śrī Vedānta Deśika Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Jīyar was born in Mukkūr on the banks of the river Ceiyyār to Vidvān Raṅgācārya Svāmī and Raṅganāyakī, in the year Manmatha in the

[] month of Āvaṇi under star Hastā (August 1895). His pūrvāśrama name was Mukkūr Rājagopālācārya Svāmī. He under_c_went his studies in the Vedapāṭhaśālā at Śrīmuṣṇam. He studied Śrīvaiṣṇava theology under renowned scholars like Taiyyār Māḍabhūṣi Śrīnivāsācārya, Śrīmuṣṇam Kṛṣṇamācārya and Naḍādūr Kṛṣṇamācārya. He also gained a strong foundation in Tarka śāstra from Śrī Cakravartyācārya Svāmī of Tillayāmbur. Śrī Kāśī Kuppusvāmī Aiyaṅgār taught him the Divyaprabandham. Soon he established himself as an able teacher and began to give religious and philosophical discourses which were appreciated by connossieur and common man alike.

However he was called upon by the 40th Jīyar to accompany him in his wide travels at the instance of the 41th Jīyar . He took charge of the affairs of the Ahobila Maṭha at Kāñcī. He became the Āsthāna Vidvān of the Ahobila Maṭha during the reign of the 42nd Jīyar.

During the brief period of the 43rd Jīyar’s reign, Śrī Rājagopālācārya accompanied him in his sojourn to North India, and when the Jīyar left for his heavenly abode in the holy land of Naimiśāraṇya, he was called upon by his disciples to take over the leadership of the Maṭha. He was reluctant at first, but he found the call of duty to be irresistible and in the year Hemalamba in the month of Kṛthikā under Śravaṇa star, he donned the ochre robes and became the pontifical head on 27.11.1957 and settled down to purposive work. Before

[] returning to the South, he visited Puṣkara where his lectures in Sanskrit and Hindi on Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra received wide acclaim. From Puṣkara he went to Tirumala and then to Tirukkaṇḍalam where he composed Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Karāvalamba Stotra. During the first 25 years of his pontificate he travelled far and wide reaching upto Rāmeśvaram in the South, widening the circle of Śrīvaiṣṇavas and strengthening the base of Śrīvaiṣṇavism by training scholars in Śrīvaiṣṇava lore and renovating Vaiṣṇava temples.

The annual Mālola Vidvatsadas became a memorable event in his time, which attracted scholars from far and wide. He was also instrumental in setting to metre the Śrībhāṣya to make it easy for memorising. He was endowed with excellent communication skills and could put across his point to the layman and philosopher alike. He has authored the following works:-

Śrī Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha Karāvalamba Stotra, Śārīraka Adhikaraṇakramabodhinī, Brahmasūtrārthapadyamālikā, Viśiṣṭādvaita-siddhāntatattvasaṅgraha, Lakṣmīnṛsiṁhaprapatti, Dayāsāgaraśataka, Pañcāmṛta stotra, Maṅgalamālikā relating to all the Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha and Sadupadeśa.

His Dayāsāgaraśatakam is in praise of Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha and the Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha who have propagated the worship of the Lord Mālola Nṛsiṁha all over the country. Written in simple Sanskrit, the poem has universal appeal. The Lord is imagined as an ocean of compassion

[] (dayāsāgara), a fire that burns the evil past of the devotees, a repository of good qualities mentioned in the Tāpanīya Upaniṣad and an all-encompassing companion who takes within his fold the prayers of Brahmins, Ceñchus the hunters, farmers and soldiers with equal pleasure. From the 53rd verse onwards Mālola journeys down the hierarchy of the Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha. The 98th verse is autobiographical.

In keeping with the vision of the founder of Ahobila Maṭha, the Jīyar was a great builder. He established a Bṛndāvana at Naimiśāraṇya for the 43rd Jīyar, built a temple at Mukkūr, Nammāḻvār’s sannidhi at Kāñcī, established a Maṭha at Pullambūtaṅguḍi, built a sannidhi for Tāyār at Iñjimeḍu, a Rājagopuram at Ahobilam, a maṇṭapa for Citra-utsava at Tiruvaḷḷūr, a temple to Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha, Lakṣmī Nārāyaṇa and Lord Hayagrīva and a Kalyāṇamaṇṭapa at Bombay, the Hṛttāpanāśinī tank at Tiruvaḷḷūr, and established Ahobila Maṭhas at Tiruvahindrapuram, Hyderabad, Bangalore and Vānamāmalai, and a large building for the Sanskrit College at Madhurāntakam. When one lists all these intellectual and administrative achievements in a saṁnyāsin’s life, a good deal of which has to be spent in the ritural worship of the presiding deity Śrī Malola Nṛsiṁha, one will be struck with a sense of wonder.

All this work pales into insignificance beside the Jīyar’s launching the construction of the Śrīraṅgam Rājagopuram when he entered his 84th year, in

[] 1979. When he intimated this idea (which was conveyed to him through a dream by Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha) to his disciples, they were wonderstruck by the magnitude of the task as also the Jīyar’s advanced age. But backed by immense reserves of will power, and armed with his engineering intuition and guided by child-like faith he went ahead with his task ordained by the Lord. Making arrangements for financial expenses which crossed the one crore mark, he personally supervised the construction work day in and day out. The residents of Śrīraṅgam will bear ample testimony to his untiring efforts which reached completion in 1985. With 13 tiers built at a cost of Rs.15 million, the Rājagopuram is the tallest tower in Asia, 165 feet in length and 150 feet in breadth and rising up to 226 feet in height.

An intellectual, a spiritual guide, a generous benefactor, a great builder, the Jīyar was also a great lover of art. Despite his tiring schedule, the Jīyar always had time to encourage artists who spread the message of bhakti (devotion). When he found that his health was failing, he called upon the āsthāna Vidvān Villivalam Kṛṣṇamācārya to take over the Maṭha affairs after granting him the ochre robes in the year Prajāpati, in the month of Aippasi (21.10.91). This Jīyar performed over 35 cāturmāsyavratas and attained heavenly abode in the year Aṅgirasa in the month of Āḍi (16.8.92). His Bṛndāvanam is at Śrīraṅgam.

[] His Taniyan reads as under:

श्रीरङ्गनाथशठकोपयतीन्द्रदृष्टं लक्ष्मींनृसिंहलज्जितकरुणैकपात्रम्। श्रीवीरराघवशठकोपमुह्यम् वेदान्तदेशिकयतीन्द्रमहं प्रपद्ये॥

45. Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika

This Svāmī was born in Villivalam in North Arcot district in Akṣaya year in the month of Kārtikai under star Uttaraṭṭādi (December 12,1926) to Paḷaveri Cakravartī Nṛsiṁhācārya Svāmī and Raṅganāyakī. His pūrvāśrama name was Kṛṣṇamācārya Svāmī. He studied at the feet of his father, but after his father’s demise at a very early age, he turned to his elder brother Nārāyaṇācārya Svāmī for guidance. He had his upākarma done by his elder brother at the appropriate time. The requisite basic education necessary for under - standing the Śrīvaiṣṇava philosophy was imparted by the Svāmī’s elder brother who was conferred the title of Vedāntavādavadūka for his proficiency in philosophy.

Śrī Kṛṣṇamācārya was a student of the Madras University passing the Nyāya Śiromaṇi Certificate in 1949 with honours, from the Madurāntakam college. He received the first prize for general proficiency. Later, he had the good fortune of learning the nyāya and mīmāṁsa śāstras at the feet of the 42nd and 43rd Jīyars of Ahobila Maṭha. He had served as Tamil Pandit in the Ramakrishna Vidyalaya, Chingleput for four years from 1956 and later, as

[] Nyāya Professor in the Śrī Ahobila Maṭha Sanskrit College, Madurāntakam till 1965. He was appointed as the Āsthāna Vidvān of the Maṭha by the 44th Jīyar in 1966 and he had been the joint-editor of the journal “Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā” (Tamil) since 1982.

Settling down at Madras Śrī Kṛṣṇamācārya had been regularly giving discourses in Śrībhāṣya, Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra, Śrīmad Rāmāyaṇa, Śrīmad Bhāgavatam, Tiruppāvai and Bhagavad Gītā at various places in the country for the past 30 years. His discourses delivered in the conventional style on the granthacatuṣṭaya were a source of perennial interest to his friends and disciples. He was a Board Member of the Ahobila Maṭha Sanskrit Vidyā Abhivardhinī Sabhā which manages the Maṭha’s Oriental High Schools at Madurāntakam and West Mambalam, as also the Sanskrit College at Madurāntakam and in this capacity his contribution is significant. His scholarly commentaries on the Upaniṣads and Viṣṇu Pūrāṇa which are published serially in the “Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā” have now been compiled and published in book form by Śrī Viśiṣṭādvaita Research Centre, Madras.

The 44th Jīyar suddenly took ill in October 1991, and immediately sent for Śrī Kṛṣṇamācārya to take up the reins of the Maṭha. His formal induction into saṁnyāsāśrama amidst traditional rituals took place on October 21st 1991. It will be significant to note that Śrī Kṛṣṇamācārya had his pañcasaṁskāra from the 42nd Jīyar, bharanyāsa under 43rd Jīyar and

[] preṣamantropadeśa from the 44th Jīyar at Śrī Ahobilam. He recalls to this day, with great veneration, his close association with these Ācāryas and mentions nostalgically many interesting ancedotes during the short period when he was called upon to attend to the personal needs of the 42nd Jīyar for sometime.165

Once the formal paṭṭābhiṣeka cermony (24.8.1992) was over, His Holiness took the āśrama name of “Śrī Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika”166 and donned the haṁsamudrā (signet ring) to execute the administrative duties which invariably form part of the pontifical head’s officaldom. He took to his task with seriousness, and the five years of his pontifical rule are enough testimony to his capacity as a good administrator. He was a scholar (vidvān) and a capable administrator (samartha).167 The Śrīkāryam of Ahobila Maṭha has listed four outstanding qualities of the present Jīyar. They are: dātṛtva, priyavaktṛtva, dhīratva and ucitajñatā.168 which qualities cannot be acquired, but are only natural to him. The Jīyar has stated in no uncertain terms after his assumption of the pontifical office that his duty was only to live up to the training, guidance and ideals of his pūrvācāryas and carry on the torch of their glorious tradition for the benefit

[] of śiṣyas and aspirants. Adhering to the guidelines laid by Svāmī Deśika, His Holiness enlightens the masses by his discourses and interesting educative writings, and performs his daily and enjoined duties through his dedicated ārādhanā to Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha - “Adhyātmagranthanirmāṇam, anekeṣāṁ ca bodhanam, arcāvatāra sevā ca.”

The Jīyar took upon himself the task of making the forest shrines of Ahobilam more accessible to the devotees, by taking Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha (utsava deity) to Ahobilam for eight times and providing the pleasure of having the darśan of the mūla and utsava idols in unison for five times starting from 26.11.1992, on 3.3.1993, 3.10.1993, 20.3.1994 and 8.10.1995. He was instrumental in constructing 32 steps leading to the Bhairava tank at Ahobilam at a cost of Rs.15,000. In March 1993, His Holiness bedecked Lord Prahlādavarada at Ahobilam with golden śaṅkha, cakra and abhayahasta, a golden crown and foot-rest and a golden yajñopavīta at a cost of Rs.17 lakhs. In October 1994, he renovated the holy tank in front of the Ahobilam temple. He performed the abhigamana and ijyārādhana for Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha in the maṇṭhapa adjoining the tank on 31.10.1996. A new chariot was ordered to be made for Lord Prahlādavarada at a cost of Rs.24 lakhs and this was presented on 5.3.1996 and on this occasion a new pathway leading to Śrī Chatravaṭa Nṛsiṁha sannidhi was laid.

[] The Jīyar’s contributions to the renovation of other divyadeśa temples are innumerable and his visit to Badrīkāśrama is a memorable one, as those who travelled in his entourage will vouchsafe. Suffice it to say, he has travelled across the length and breadth of India169 in his onerous task of carrying out the divine command of Lord Nṛsiṁha. His literary contribution is also very significant. Noteworthy among his works is the Sudhīpriyā, a nithyagrantha commentary on the Śrīvaiṣṇavasadācāranirṇaya of Śrī Raṅganātha Yatīndra, the 26th pontiff. It took nearly seven valuable years to compile this work and its speaks volumes for the Jīyar’s Ācārya bhakthi because he had undertaken this work at the instance of the 42nd Jīyar. He has performed four cāturmāsya vratas. The establishment of several Trusts to take care of the various activities of the Maṭha is a signficant event during the Jīyar’s pontifical rule. They are: the Save Trust, Smart Trust, Samrāṭ Trust, Viśiṣṭādvaita Research Centre and Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā Trust.170 In the midst of his very busy schedule the Jīyar is presently writing a commentary on Śrīmad Rahasyatrayasāra which is being published serially in the Śrī Nṛsiṁha Priyā.

Carrying the mantle of his forbears in propagating the Śrīvaiṣṇava religion and philosophy, His Holiness, the 45th Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha

[] demonstrates how spirituality and monasticism can be effectively practised in a secular society.

His Taniyan reads as under:-

श्रीमदूरङ्गशठारिसंयमिधुरन्धरलब्धधृगान्तसद्व्यं श्रीमद्वीररघुद्वहस्ययमिहृब्जात्स्थायिपादार विन्दाश्रयम्। श्रीमद्देवयदेशिकम्पतेः कारुण्यवीक्षास्पदं सेवे रघुपरीणशासनवशं नारायण योगिनम्॥

The above is a brief description of the lives of the saints of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha. The onerous task started by Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa is continuing into the future also.

[]

SELECT WORKS

A STUDY OF SELECT WORKS OF THE JĪYARS OF ŚRĪ AHOBILA MAṬHA

An attempt is made in this chapter to present a brief study of some works of the Pontiffs of Śrī Ahobila Maṭha. The works are selected on the basis of their literary and philosophical importance. Smaller stotras like daśakas, aṣṭottaraśatas and maṅgalāśāsanas are not taken into consideration. Some of the works are highly scholarly disputations, some are elucidatory of important concepts like puruṣakāra and rahasyas, while some others are commentarial, expounding basic texts like the Śrībhāṣya and Gītārthasaṅgraha. As many as 25 works of the Pontiffs have been studied in this chapter. Some of the works are in the form of palm-leaf / paper manuscripts while a majority of them is available in print. The fact that the Pontiffs could find time to compose excellent treatises inspite of their busy schedule of ritual worship of the presiding deity Śrī Mālola Nṛsiṁha, temple renovations, periodical tours and so on, makes the study all the more inspiring and interesting.

[]

Yajussandhyāvandanabhāṣya

171

The author, Śrī Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra Mahādeśika, second Jīyar begins his Bhāṣya by paying his obeisance to Lord Lakṣmī Nṛsiṁha the presiding deity at Ahobilam and then to his guru and predecessor, Śrī Ādi Vaṇ Śaṭhakopa Svāmī by whose grace, the import of Vedas was made as clear as the fruit in one’s palm. This echoes the idea expressed in the Śvetāśvataropaniṣad172 which stresses the importance of Bhagavad bhakti and Ācārya bhakti in elucidating the inner meaning of the mantras.

The author declares at the outset that thousands of commentaries are available for the Sandhyāvandana mantras and states that the present work comments on these mantras from the Vedāntic point of view.173

The author points out that the word Devatā, whenever it occurs in the mantra must be taken to refer to Lord Nārāyaṇa only, since the Pāñcarātra texts declare thus - “Paramātmā devatā”, and the paramātmā is none other

[] than Lord Nārāyaṇa Himself. Since the upaniṣadic passages have also been interpreted in the Śrīvaiṣṇava tradition as implying the supremacy and the causal character of Lord Nārāyaṇa, the present body of literature namely the Sandhyāvandana mantra should also be interpreted in the same light.

The author profusely quotes from the Brahma Sūtras, Upaniṣads, Purāṇas and Bhagavad Gītā to elucidate his interpretations. For example, the word āpas found in the portion of the mantra - āpo janayathā ca naḥ (p. 6) is interpreted by our author to mean Lord Viṣṇu who has the waters as His Body. The nāmarūpavyākaraṇa Śruti in Chāndogya (section vi) has been interpreted by Śrī Rāmānuja174 to mean that all words referring to living and non-living entities must imply only the Supreme Being, since all these form the body of the Lord, and since the Lord exists in all these entities as the inner soul (antaryāmin). Even holy rivers like the Ganges are adorable because of their association with the Lord and the very characteristic of sanctity has been imparted to them by the Lord Himself.175

Likewise the word “sūrya” in the mantra starting, sūryaśca mā manyuśca … is interpretated by Śrī Nārāyaṇa Yatīndra to mean Lord Nārāyaṇa

[] only.176 This is in accordance with the Śrībhāṣya on the Brahma Sūtra (I, i, 21): antastaddharmopadeśāt.

On the same lines, the author proceeds to explain the term Varuṇa to mean Lord Nārāyaṇa (p-42). Finally the mantra hails Varuṇa and prays that all sins be destroyed:

सर्वां तां विश्व जिधिवे देव! अथाते स्याम वरुण प्रियासः।

and this destroyer of sin is none other than Śrīman Nārāyaṇa.

This has been rendered into Maṇipravāḷa by the 42nd Jīyar of Ahobila Maṭha. In the introduction, he summarises the necessity of performing sandhyāvandana by all people belonging to the three Varṇas namely Brāhmins, Kṣatriyas and Vaiśyas, and states that one who does not perform this nityakarma is not eligible to perform any karma at all. (anarhaḥ sarvakarmasu). He also states that he has written in Maṇipravāḷa style to enable laymen to understand the real import of the mantras which in turn will enable them to perform their daily duties. This vyākhyā makes easy reading and is quite useful for laymen of Sanskrit language.

[]

Nyāsa-viṁśati Vyākhyā

177

The doctrine of prapatti as expounded in the Śrīvaiṣṇava system of philosophy, with its catholicity of approach is recommended to all irrespective of distinctions of caste; and this has taken the doctrine to the lowest of the low, to layman and woman alike. Vedānta Deśika’s Nyāsa-viṁśati is a metrical composition in 22 verses dealing with this doctrine for which Deśika himself has written a commentary. However the author of this explanatory treatise, Śrī Nārāyaṇa Muni (2nd Jīyar) feels that Deśika’s commentary is not simple enough and hence he has penned this work.

Beginning with the term Sat-sampradāya178 the author offers a couple of interpretations. It means the tradition as established by Yāmuna and other ācāryas; the secret teachings of the tradition imparted by guru to śiṣya (rahasyajñāta), it or may refer to noble descent (satkulaprasūti). The term īpset in the desiderative form suggests that the whole process is something obligatory (niyogavidhi).179 The characteristics of the guru and qualifications of the disciple are enumerated. The teacher imparts learning to the disciple which is in fact vidyā-janma and hence the disciple is born again.

[] The term mām and ekam in the Carama śloka are important, according to the author. Explaining v.16 of the Nyāsa Viṁśati, the author feels that the word ekam in particular precludes prapatti from the scope of upāya; and exhibits the oneness (aikya) of upāya and upeya; it may be interpreted as referring to the Lord as the one who can confer all human ends, that He does not require anything else but nyāsa as a pretext (vyājamātram) to save the devotees; or it may be taken to mean the Lord as the most important means of mokṣa. Nārāyaṇa Muni makes an interesting observation as to whether ekam includes Śrī - His Consort or not. The answer is that Lord Viṣṇu in eternal association with Śrī forms a single unitary principle i.e. the supreme God-head. This has been indicated by Vedāntadeśika by the use of the term Śrīsakha.180 Explaining the sādhyopāya, the author states that prapatti is śaraṇāgati and quotes from the Śrībhāṣya181 where Rāmānuja uses the term śaraṇāgati.

Explaining v.19, the author states that one should give up vidhi and niṣedha types of acts and should perform only such acts by which one does not incur anartha. Now and then one has to do prāyaścitta. This itself is explained as prapatti by Śrī Deśika. The ultimate advice to prapannas is that bhakti etc., should be asked for only from the Lord or His associates

[] (bhaktyādikam bhagavataḥ tadīyebhyo yācet).182 Acts for peace, health and strength should be done invoking Lord Viṣṇu only, to the exclusion of other gods like Brahmā, Indra (śāntipauṣṭikādikam ca bhagavantamuddhiśyaiva kuryāt, na brahmārudrāgnyādikam)

The ājñā (compulsory) and anujñā (permitted) duties are discussed in the commentary of v. 20.
